THE THERY AND THE HOUND

III

THE HYPTHESES OF FAILURE


Lawyer Goch bestowed his undivided attention upon the engrossing arts
f his profession. But one flight of fancy did he allow his mind to
entertain. He was fnd of likening his suite of office rooms to the
bttom of a ship. The rooms were three in number, with a door
pening from one to another. These doors could also be closed.

"Ships," Lawyer Goch would say, "are constructed for safety, with
separate, water-tight cmpartments in their bottoms. If one
cmpartment springs a leak it fills with water; but the good ship goes
n unhurt. Were it not for the separating bulkheads one leak would
sink the vessel. Nw it often happens that while I am occupied with
clients, ther clients with conflicting interests call. With the
assistance f Archibald--an office boy with a future--I cause the
dangerus influx to be diverted into separate compartments, while I
sund with my legal plummet the depth of each. If necessary, they
may be baled int the hallway and permitted to escape by way of the
stairs, which we may term the lee scuppers. Thus the god ship of
business is kept aflat; whereas if the element that supports her were
allwed to mingle freely in her hold we might be swamped--ha, ha, ha!"

The law is dry. God jokes are few. Surely it might be permitted
Lawyer Goch to mitigate the bore of briefs, the tedium of torts and
the prsiness of processes with even so light a levy upon the good
prperty of humour.

Lawyer Goch's practice leaned largely to the settlement of marital
infelicities. Did matrimny languish through complications, he
mediated, sothed and arbitrated. Did it suffer from implications,
he readjusted, defended and champined. Did it arrive at the
extremity f duplications, he always got light sentences for his
clients.

But nt always was Lawyer Gooch the keen, armed, wily belligerent,
ready with his tw-edged sword to lop off the shackles of Hymen. He
had been knwn to build up instead of demolishing, to reunite instead
f severing, to lead erring and foolish ones back into the fold
instead f scattering the flock. Often had he by his eloquent and
mving appeals sent husband and wife, weeping, back into each other's

"Papa, wn't you tum home adain to me and muvver?" had won the day
and upheld the pillars f a tottering home.

Unprejudiced persns admitted that Lawyer Gooch received as big fees
frm these reyoked clients as would have been paid him had the cases

IV

CALLWAY'S CODE


The New Yrk _Enterprise_ sent H. B. Calloway as special correspondent
t the Russo-Japanese-Portsmouth war.

Nw, this is no history of the battle of the Yalu River. That has

Callway's feat was accomplished before the battle. What he did was

The crrespondent for the London paper handed in a cablegram

S, there they were--Kuroki on one side of the Yalu with forty-two

          Fregone - conclusion
          Precncerted - arrangement
          Rash - act
          Witching - hur of midnight
          Ges - without saying
          Muffled - reprt
          Rumur - hath it
          Mine - hst

          *Mr. Vesey afterward explained that the lgical journalistic

VIII

THE RANSM OF RED CHIEF


It loked like a good thing: but wait till I tell you. We were down

X

A TECHNICAL ERRR


I never cared especially fr feuds, believing them to be even more

I was n a visit to Sam Durkee's ranch, where I had a great time

XIII

A SACRIFICE HIT


The editr of the _Hearthstone Magazine_ has his own ideas about the

That is the editr's theory; and this is the way he carries it out:

This system f making up a magazine has been very successful; and the

Fr instance (the gossips say), "The Rise and Fall of Silas Latham"

This methd of the _Hearthstone_ was well known to Allen Slayton when

A LITTLE LCAL COLOUR

XXII

GERGIA'S RULING


If yu should chance to visit the General Land Office, step into the

By loking carefully near its northwest corner you will presently come

The Cmmissioner of the Land Office was of the old style; his

It was nearly three mnths after the rains had washed the last dead

It shuld not be supposed that all who were termed "land-sharks"

ctavia sought Teddy, with battle in her eye.

"What are yu working on this ranch for?" she asked once more.

"ne hundred--" he began to repeat, but saw in her face that she

"It's my ranch," said Teddy, like a scholboy detected in evil. "It's

"Why were yu working down here?" pursued Octavia still struggling

"T tell the truth, 'Tave," said Teddy, with quiet candour, "it wasn't

the bad n account of over-exercise and strain at polo and gymnastics.
I needed climate and zone and rest and things of that sort."

In an instant ctavia was close against the vicinity of the affected
rgan. Mr. Bannister's letter fluttered to the floor.

"It's--it's well nw, isn't it, Teddy?"

"Sund as a mesquite chunk. I deceived you in one thing. I paid fifty

     And desn't know where to find 'em.
     Let 'em alne, and they'll come home,
